<div id="review_1368316225" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1368316225" />
    <a title="Dannii Elle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle"><img alt="Dannii Elle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508499419p2/44487975.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1368316225?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dannii Elle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dannii Elle" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle">Dannii Elle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781407121116" href="/book/show/9718047-forever">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=fantastic-fabrications">fantastic-fabrications</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=romantic-recollections">romantic-recollections</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1368316225" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16003904094086617036">So, I think it is only fair to state that I had average feelings on the first book in this series and also really disliked the second book, before beginning this third instalment. Going in to this I was less than enthusiastic, which may have hindered my enjoyment before I even began. Why begin a book I was so sure I wasn't going to enjoy, you ask? Because I'm clearly a glutton for punishment with minor OCD about finishing a book series.<br/><br/>I did find this a vast improvement from the previous book, w</span>
  <span id="freeText16003904094086617036" style="display:none">So, I think it is only fair to state that I had average feelings on the first book in this series and also really disliked the second book, before beginning this third instalment. Going in to this I was less than enthusiastic, which may have hindered my enjoyment before I even began. Why begin a book I was so sure I wasn't going to enjoy, you ask? Because I'm clearly a glutton for punishment with minor OCD about finishing a book series.<br /><br />I did find this a vast improvement from the previous book, where literally NOTHING happened, but there was still far too much angst for me to immerse myself in the story. Sam and Grace are the most melodramatic protagonists, and I could not care less about their whiny and repetitive perspectives. The previous side characters, that continued to be given a larger role as the series progressed, were this book's saving grace. Isabel and Cole each had so much sass and seeing their burgeoning romance and growing character developments felt truly special, opposed to the instantaneous attraction and endless endearments uttered by Sam and Grace.<br /><br />The actual plot was accessible, if pretty predictable, but not completely horrible and, as before, Stiefvater's writing continued to shine. This story, as a whole, is just not for me, but I have not written myself off from trying more of Stiefvater's renowned book series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16003904094086617036" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer13278048561093641767">Ms. Stiefvater completely outdid herself writing Forever. The characters that we met, loved, and sometimes despised,in Shiver and Linger are more vibrant than ever. We get to know Isabel and Cole much better in Forever, and that knowledge makes them each a bit more endearing. The relationship between Grace and Sam still feels new and exciting, yet undoubtedly true and well...."forever" love. This stunning conclusion moves faster than even Shiver and Linger did, sometimes I wanted to find out wha</span>
  <span id="freeText13278048561093641767" style="display:none">Ms. Stiefvater completely outdid herself writing Forever. The characters that we met, loved, and sometimes despised,in Shiver and Linger are more vibrant than ever. We get to know Isabel and Cole much better in Forever, and that knowledge makes them each a bit more endearing. The relationship between Grace and Sam still feels new and exciting, yet undoubtedly true and well...."forever" love. This stunning conclusion moves faster than even Shiver and Linger did, sometimes I wanted to find out what happened next so badly, that I'm afraid I missed some of the amazing and unique details that I love so much in Ms. Stiefvater's novels. Along with her many other fans, I have been anxiously awaiting this book, and I was not, for one milli-second, disappointed. This was totally true to Ms. Stiefvater---not everything is tied up with a pretty bow, the good guy doesn't always win, and the bad guy isn't always apprehended....but the reader is completely satisfied!<br /><br />I have purchased all three books as a gift for my niece, and I will pre-order another Scorpio Races, just for her.</span>

<div id="review_91217890" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/91217890" />
    <a title="Amelia, free market Puritan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan"><img alt="Amelia, free market Puritan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508223427p2/1852293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/91217890?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amelia, free market Puritan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amelia, free market Puritan" href="/user/show/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan">Amelia, free market Puritan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=bea11">bea11</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=annoying-characters">annoying-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=just-the-worst">just-the-worst</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=series-books">series-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=ya-kids-teen">ya-kids-teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer91217890" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17653010150120613420">We apparently have a different opinion on what "forever" means. :S <br/><br/>First and foremost, To Whomever wrote that synopsis or whatever up at the top, "thrilling" is not a word that I would use to describe the first 250 pages...<br/><br/>Basically, I did not like this installment. More often than not it was a bore and a chore to get through. And I hate typing that! <i>Shiver</i> is still one of my favorite novels ever, and I did enjoy <i>Linger</i>, though not quite as much. This whole series and its progression really got </span>
  <span id="freeText17653010150120613420" style="display:none">We apparently have a different opinion on what "forever" means. :S <br /><br />First and foremost, To Whomever wrote that synopsis or whatever up at the top, "thrilling" is not a word that I would use to describe the first 250 pages...<br /><br />Basically, I did not like this installment. More often than not it was a bore and a chore to get through. And I hate typing that! <i>Shiver</i> is still one of my favorite novels ever, and I did enjoy <i>Linger</i>, though not quite as much. This whole series and its progression really got me wondering why it is that nearly EVERY non-contemp YA book is being turned into a trilogy/series, because with each book I felt a little less magic. A little less pizazz.<br /><br />Why specifically did <i>Forever</i> not work for me? First of all, it seemed overly dramatic in a way that <i>Shiver</i> and <i>Linger</i> were not. If you thought that any of the first two books were slow or prone to melodrama (as I know that others have said), then in my opinion, you may find <i>Forever</i> challenging. Unlike most finale books in a series, it is not more fast-paced. In my opinion, it actually seemed slower. There were several periods throughout most of the chapters when the characters - especially Sam - would have these really long, drawn out personal reflections. Flashbacks would occur randomly, and I'd say for about the first 200 pages, the plot just kind of meandered along. Characters would drift in and out of contact, and oh the angst. Yeah, the series has always been dramatic, emotional too, but I never thought the angst was overdone until now. Sam - whom I absolutely adored in <i>Shiver</i> - just kind of moped around and really didn't do much of anything but feel sorry for himself. Cole sat around thinking about how his life used to be. Grace kept shifting and bolting. One or two times and it's dramatic, but four times? Then it just gets downright annoying, I'm sorry to say. I don't like it when authors have things happen over and over again with the same results. In my playbook, that's repetition, not suspense or excitement.<br /><br />For me, though, I could have forgotten the slow start and the aggravating parts but for the ending. Guys, when you hear the word "forever," what do you think of? Maybe if you're like me, you hear Squints from <i>The Sandlot</i> pulling out the word like "foooooorrreeeevvveeeerrrr" over and over (haha). But you think of something that has closure, right? For me, it's practically false advertising when you've got the final book in a series titled something permanent sounding like <i>Forever</i>, and the ending doesn't have a whole lot of closure. I get it, really I do. I get that it's bad to give teen characters any kind of "permanent closure," because after all, they're only 18, right? For me, though, it does not work to feed me a story, a fictional story (that really is not in the least bit obligated to reflect, endorse, or champion "reality") in which characters have this serious, mature, real-deal love...and then turn around and leave the ending open-ended. Did I expect the kind of ending that was found in the epilogue of <i>Deathly Hallows</i>? Well, maybe. And really, who knows better how to end a [modern] YA series than JK Rowing?<br />I also kind of took issue with the last chapter in general, really. Grace, to me, made a decision that seemed extremely out-of-character for her, given her relationship and previous history with Sam. All I'm wanting is for a series ending to accurately reflect the series as a whole, and here, it was my perception that the author pulled back a little and went with a more "realistic" ending. And that just didn't work for me in a series like this.<br /><br />I realize that was a really long, lengthy (and highly opinionated) explanation, but I do feel like I need to explain what it was that left me disappointed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17653010150120613420" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_153607703" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/153607703" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/153607703?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=werewolves">werewolves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=i-totally-saw-that-coming">i-totally-saw-that-coming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=alternating-povs">alternating-povs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=best-characters">best-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=could-have-been-better">could-have-been-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=i-liked-it">i-liked-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer153607703" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3331150894178332969"><br/>Actual rating: 3.5 stars<br/><br/>In a recent Q&A discussion, Maggie Stiefvater mentioned that she loves to write books that will make you cry your little eyes out. And I did...for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6068551.Shiver__The_Wolves_of_Mercy_Falls__1_' title='Shiver (The Wolves of Mercy Falls #1) by Maggie Stiefvater' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shiver</a>. I'm not sure what it is, but <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6654313.Linger__The_Wolves_of_Mercy_Falls___2_' title='Linger (The Wolves of Mercy Falls, #2) by Maggie Stiefvater' rel='nofollow noopener'>Linger</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9409458.Forever__Wolves_of_Mercy_Falls___3_' title='Forever (Wolves of Mercy Falls, #3) by Maggie Stiefvater' rel='nofollow noopener'>Forever</a> just did not string up the same emotions. Did I enjoy them? Sure. But the magic just wasn't there like it was in Shiver. <br/><br/><i>Forever</i> picks up a few weeks after the events in <i>Linger</i>. Sam is pretty much going through the motions until Grace shifts back into human form. The new t</span>
  <span id="freeText3331150894178332969" style="display:none"><br />Actual rating: 3.5 stars<br /><br />In a recent Q&amp;A discussion, Maggie Stiefvater mentioned that she loves to write books that will make you cry your little eyes out. And I did...for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6068551.Shiver__The_Wolves_of_Mercy_Falls__1_" title="Shiver (The Wolves of Mercy Falls #1) by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">Shiver</a>. I'm not sure what it is, but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6654313.Linger__The_Wolves_of_Mercy_Falls___2_" title="Linger (The Wolves of Mercy Falls, #2) by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">Linger</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9409458.Forever__Wolves_of_Mercy_Falls___3_" title="Forever (Wolves of Mercy Falls, #3) by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">Forever</a> just did not string up the same emotions. Did I enjoy them? Sure. But the magic just wasn't there like it was in Shiver. <br /><br /><i>Forever</i> picks up a few weeks after the events in <i>Linger</i>. Sam is pretty much going through the motions until Grace shifts back into human form. The new threat in the novel is Isabel's father attempting to get the wolves taken off the protective list and Shelby, the crazy she-wolf, attacking and murdering new pack members. <br /><br />Now, while the sparks didn't exactly fly between <i>Forever</i> and I, there were a few things that I did really enjoy about this book:<br /><br />1. Maggie has such beautiful prose. It is undeniable. I LOVED it. Her writing style calls to me and speaks my soul's language. I think this is most quotes I have "liked" from just one book. I could quote her books all day long because it is so poetic. She just has a wonderful way with words that can invoke so much feeling with so few words. This book can easily be described as "emo," but never comes across as too much teen angst. The feelings the characters displayed seemed very realistic and believable to me. <br /><br />2. Cole. Need I say more? Dude is made of that special flavor of awesome sauce. His witty, comedic voice was the fudge icing on my German chocolate cake. YUM. <br /><br />3. Grace's relationship with her parents. In a lot of YA novels these days, parents are conveniently out of the picture while out hero or heroine is running of saving the world. Usually, this is unrealistic. However, I really liked how this was handled in this series. Yes, Grace's parents are not around, BUT this is acknowledged that it wasn't a good thing or normal. In fact, Grace confronts her parents in <i>Forever</i> about this. I think this was important to address because Grace needed her parents and was forced to grow up without them. <br /><br />4. Isabel's feelings about Jack. They were so spot on for how a sibling feels about losing the other. So accurate. <br /><br />One main problem I had with this book was that every time something big or interesting was about to happen to one of the characters, it immediately switches to another character's POV. As a result, a lot of the action happens "off-screen" and we are later told about it through another POV. I found this irritating. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[For example: I would have really liked to see more of Cole's experiments, the science behind the Wolf, and most importantly, Beck's capture! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I'm not entirely sure how I liked the ending. On one hand, I think it is a very realistic end and it works. But on the other, I feel like it just *ends*. It didn't really disappoint me, but it didn't satisfy me either.<br /><br />All in all, this series was a good read and I'm really looking forward to future works from Maggie Stiefvater.<br /><br />More reviews and more at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3331150894178332969" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_74487291" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/74487291" />
    <a title="~Tina~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2594672-tina"><img alt="~Tina~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411474324p2/2594672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/74487291?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~Tina~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~Tina~" href="/user/show/2594672-tina">~Tina~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=wolves-shapeshiftes">wolves-shapeshiftes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer74487291" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1428197873631824789"><b>:Spoilers:</b><br/><br/>This series has been one long roller-coaster of pure emotional agony from the very first book till it hits the very last page in the third and final installment in, <b>Forever</b>. <br/>We have shared epic love, sorrow and an adventure with these characters that I have never had the pleasure to do with other books. The writing is truly like a piece of art work. I'm sad to see this gorgeous series go and while I had my moments, both the good and the bad, these books will always be treasured in my h</span>
  <span id="freeText1428197873631824789" style="display:none"><b>:Spoilers:</b><br /><br />This series has been one long roller-coaster of pure emotional agony from the very first book till it hits the very last page in the third and final installment in, <b>Forever</b>. <br />We have shared epic love, sorrow and an adventure with these characters that I have never had the pleasure to do with other books. The writing is truly like a piece of art work. I'm sad to see this gorgeous series go and while I had my moments, both the good and the bad, these books will always be treasured in my heart.<br /><br />I <i>swear</i>, there is nothing like reading a Maggie Stiefvater book. Her whimsical words are like magic to a drowning person, desperate to finally get what we've been craving for nearly a year. <br />Maggie's writing is pure art, pure poetry and I'll never get tired of it.<br /><br />I love these characters, but I think Cole should take a bow in this book. I actually got to liking him much more in this round, he's still erratic and a bit of a punk, but I admired his dedication and strength and when honest, is truly something to witness. Isabel will always be a character that I will enjoy, I love her stubbornness and fire. I wish we had more scenes between Sam and Grace in the beginning. The wait was truly painful. But what moments we did get were well worth the wait.<br />I don't have to much to say about Grace's parents, except that they got more then they deserved in my opinion. As for Beck? &lt;3!!!!!!<br />Sam and Grace is a couple that will always be unforgettable in my eyes and heart. They have such a passion and such a love that people only dream about. I have never wanted so much for one couple before and never knew one that deserved it as much as these two.<br /><br />Reading this book was slow exhausting torture, but in the sweetest way possible. My stomach was in knots wanting so desperately for it to turn out with a HEA, almost needing it to the point of physical pain. <br />I kid you not.<br />Ever page was laced with a teasing tone of uncertainty which made the experience that much thicker, richer and earned an appreciation I didn't think could exist even more then what I already feel for it.<br /><br />As for the ending, well, I feel that I should be truthful. Was I satisfied? Yes and...no. I'm content, lets put it that way, but I feel that the biggest question still lingered and I hate that I'll <i>forever</i> be thinking about it every time I visit this world again. It ended on the tone that pretty much described the entire series. With mystery and suspense and above all, hope. So if your looking for an ending with absolute closure, you wont find it here my friends. I wish there was a few more pages or a few last final lines that would make it all okay. But there wasn't and apart of me is very sad about that.<br />So...I'm just going to have to hold on to what Cole wisely said;<br /><br /><i>"The thing I was beginning to figure out about Sam and Grace, the thing about Sam not being able to function without her, was that that sort of love only worked when you were sure both people would always be around for each other. If one half of the equation left, or died, or was slightly less perfect in their love, it became the most tragic, pathetic story invented, laughable in it's absurdity. Without Grace, Sam was a joke without a punch line."</i><br /><br />...and so with that, I believe Grace and Sam do get their happily ever after...cause it would be wrong to imagine anything less.<br /><br />They will be missed.<br /><br />Congrats to Maggie on the success of her <i>The Wolves of Mercy Falls</i> series. I will never forget them and look forward to your next new adventure.<br /><br />Bravo!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1428197873631824789" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2267950402" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2267950402" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43846663-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574280006p2/43846663.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2267950402?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/43846663-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43846663-amanda?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43846663-amanda?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43846663-amanda?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43846663-amanda?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2267950402" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4238197909026839890">**3.5 STARS**<br/><br/><i>Forever</i> by Maggie Stiefvater is the conclusion to the <i>Wolves of Mercy Falls</i> series. Its always hard to review a finale because there's so much to be said about how everything turned out. Honestly, I feel like I just became a wolf like Grace and Sam and all my human thoughts have abandoned me. I can only think in short thoughts right now so I'm just going to go with it. <br/><br/><b><u>What I Liked</u>:</b><br/><br/>1. The imagery was top notch as usual. Maggie Stiefvater has a way of describing things that makes the</span>
  <span id="freeText4238197909026839890" style="display:none">**3.5 STARS**<br /><br /><i>Forever</i> by Maggie Stiefvater is the conclusion to the <i>Wolves of Mercy Falls</i> series. Its always hard to review a finale because there's so much to be said about how everything turned out. Honestly, I feel like I just became a wolf like Grace and Sam and all my human thoughts have abandoned me. I can only think in short thoughts right now so I'm just going to go with it. <br /><br /><b><u>What I Liked</u>:</b><br /><br />1. The imagery was top notch as usual. Maggie Stiefvater has a way of describing things that makes them feel so visceral and exciting. <br /><br />2. <b>Isabel and Cole are life!</b> They are infinitely fascinating characters and I can't wait to read their spin off novel. <br /><br />3. Sam and Grace being in wolf love is the most adorable thing I ever read. I'm just picturing them touching snouts and its wonderful.<br /><br />4. The open-ended, bittersweet ending really fit the series as a whole. I don't usually like endings like this but in this case, there was a strange sense of hope about the whole thing that I really loved. <br /><br /><b><u>What I Didn't Like</u>:</b><br /><br />1. Shelby is just a monster and I hate her. I wish there were more chapters than just one from her perspective. Maybe it would have given me some kind of empathy for her. <br /><br />2. The pacing felt off. I don't know... at times it felt stagnant and slow and at other times it was everything happening all at once. However, it wasn't as stagnant as <i>Linger</i> so there's that at least. <br /><br />3. There wasn't nearly enough Isabel and Cole chapters!<br /><br />4. Why are all the parents in Mercy Falls a bunch of buttholes? Occasionally, I sort of liked Isabel's mom but she's not winning a parent of the year award by any means. <br /><br />Overall, I enjoyed the finale to the <i>Wolves of Mercy Falls</i> series. I got what I needed out of it to feel like the story was complete and I was happy with how things turned out. There are some loose ends that were never addressed but they were just the minor practical things like are they selling Beck's house and moving to the lodge or what are they going to do in the future for money and whatnot. Really, I'm more excited that the spin off is a primarily Isabel and Cole story. I can't wait to get into that one. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4238197909026839890" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_224302627" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/224302627" />
    <a title="Taneika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5591031-taneika"><img alt="Taneika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564410672p2/5591031.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/224302627?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Taneika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Taneika" href="/user/show/5591031-taneika">Taneika</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer224302627" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3753182490778552750"><b>More of my reviews can be found at <a href='http://flippingthroughthepages00.blogspot.com/ ' rel='nofollow noopener'>Flipping Through the Pages</a>!</b><br/><br/>This is going to be an incredibly difficult review.<br/><br/>Shiver had me interested, however it wasn't my favourite, Linger was even better and again, Maggie had me a snivelling wreck throughout the book. As for Forever? Oh, I wanted to love it, I really really did. There were bits I loved but honestly, my emotions were ALL OVER THE PLACE whilst reading that I just can't love it the way I loved Linger especially.<br/><br/>Forever explores Isabel's and </span>
  <span id="freeText3753182490778552750" style="display:none"><b>More of my reviews can be found at <a href="http://flippingthroughthepages00.blogspot.com/ " rel="nofollow noopener">Flipping Through the Pages</a>!</b><br /><br />This is going to be an incredibly difficult review.<br /><br />Shiver had me interested, however it wasn't my favourite, Linger was even better and again, Maggie had me a snivelling wreck throughout the book. As for Forever? Oh, I wanted to love it, I really really did. There were bits I loved but honestly, my emotions were ALL OVER THE PLACE whilst reading that I just can't love it the way I loved Linger especially.<br /><br />Forever explores Isabel's and Cole's relationship, this really pleased me because Isabel and Cole are two of my favourite literary characters ever. They're both just so messed up in the head and real that I can't help but want the two to hurry up and be in a relationship. I was once again impressed with Isabel's character, due to the fact that she actually gave a shit that her brother died. In alot of YA novels, a character's family member or friend may die, and said character then finds true love and forgets all about their lost loved one. This seriously pisses me off and I'm so so glad that even though Isabel's feelings for Cole were blossoming, she didn't forget the fact that she just happened to lose her brother a few months earlier. Her inner dialogue really made me sympathise with her because in reality, which Wolves of Mercy Falls manages to portray, this very real depression happens.<br /><br />As for Cole, I really grew to love Cole. His presence sort of annoyed me in Linger because I didn't know why he was even in the story and I thought that he was just added as a balm for Isabel's pain. However, Cole proved to be extremely intelligent and emotional in this installment and reminded me of many guys I know - not the whole rockstar thing, but the hiding the true emotion thing.<br /><br />In regards to Grace and Sam's relationship. I was disappointed. If you happened to turn into a wolf and hadn't seen your love for months on end, would you not be DESPERATE to find them? I mean, I know Grace was a wolf and wolves forget their human memories and feelings and all that jazz but <b>AFTER SHE TURNS BACK INTO A HUMAN</b>, she <b>FORGETS</b> his name. WTF. She redeemed herself in my eyes when she finally went off her face at her dimwitted parents - her father in particular. As for Sam, well, if you've read my reviews of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/199730662" rel="nofollow noopener">Shiver</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6654313-linger" rel="nofollow noopener">Linger</a> on Goodreads or on <a>my blog</a>, you will know how much of a Sam fangirl I am. That hasn't changed.<br /><br />This installment took me an incredible amount of time to get into, I was over halfway the book when last night, I decided I was going to finished this series and because I found myself more invested in the book then I had the last couple of days. I stayed up until <u>3 AM</u>. The ball finally started rolling and I really got into this installment <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[when Officer Koenig figured out the wolf situation <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. When the ball started rolling, the tears started to flow. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Beck and Sam's conversation was heartbreaking and this quote undone me... <i>"And it that split second, as Beck's face turned toward the ceiling, his eyes unchanging, I saw my own face"</i>. Really, this entire scene had me in tears, but that last sentence made me BAWL. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. At one point, after Cole was done waiting for the wolves to come and when he saw Sam and Shelby, I went crazy. These last few chapters had my emotions swinging one way to the other and I had emotional whiplash. One minute I was crying, then I was happy, the next minute I was angry at Maggie for ONE particular scene <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I mean "KILLING" COLE in such a terrible, fast way, and "KILLING" HIM FULLSTOP. Also, I saw Beck's death coming but I didn't start crying until Sam was on the ground <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. After said particular scene, I felt numb and angry. I didn't even cry when I normally would have because I was in shock. THEN Maggie pulls another stunt, which made me happy again <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Cole actually living, I sort of expected it but it still made me immensely happy <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />The entire second half of this installment had me going nuts with emotion and then, it just ended. Just like that. I was so so incredibly disappointed and I was extremely upset with the way it ended, because it didn't leave me with any closure, it just left me wondering if I had a dodgy copy and if pages were missing. I mean, <i>I STAYED UP UNTIL 3AM FOR IT TO END LIKE THAT?</i>. Due to that, and the slow beginning, it really pains me to give this a three star rating because if it ended differently, this series could have easily been up there with some of my other favourites. I'm afraid I can't say that anymore.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3753182490778552750" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_75549603" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/75549603" />
    <a title="Brigid ✩" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/886144-brigid"><img alt="Brigid ✩" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581869052p2/886144.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/75549603?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brigid ✩" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brigid ✩" href="/user/show/886144-brigid">Brigid ✩</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=werewolves">werewolves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer75549603" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9452109339556181034">In a nutshell: I really liked it. Not quite as much as the first two books, but I still liked it.<br/><br/>There were a lot of things I really appreciated about this series. I'm not a huge fan of paranormal romance because they all tend to be exactly the same, so I like that the Wolves of Mercy Falls had its unique traits. For example, Maggie Stiefvater actually bothered to create her own werewolf mythology/rules/etc. and not just, "I'm a werewolf ... just because." I really like the world she created and</span>
  <span id="freeText9452109339556181034" style="display:none">In a nutshell: I really liked it. Not quite as much as the first two books, but I still liked it.<br /><br />There were a lot of things I really appreciated about this series. I'm not a huge fan of paranormal romance because they all tend to be exactly the same, so I like that the Wolves of Mercy Falls had its unique traits. For example, Maggie Stiefvater actually bothered to create her own werewolf mythology/rules/etc. and not just, "I'm a werewolf ... just because." I really like the world she created and what she did with her idea.<br /><br />Secondly, I really like her writing style. It's kind of a shame that her first popular series had to be a werewolf series because it caused people to go into it thinking, "Oh, this is going to be exactly like Twilight" and therefore losing respect for her. And yeah, there is a lot of mushy-gushy stuff in the series. But I see a lot of potential in Stiefvater's writing and ideas and I expect even greater things to come from her in the future.<br /><br />Thirdly, I'm so glad there was no love triangle in these books. I'm so effing sick of love triangles that the very idea often makes me want to explode. When I first heard about Cole coming into the series I was like, "Oh no ..." But thankfully, he was not a threat to the main relationship. I really liked him and Isabel as a couple. And I like that Grace is dedicated to Sam and not going around, leading on every boy who comes along. I mean, she's not the greatest character on the planet, but at least she's a somewhat better role model than many YA heroines (if you could even call them that) out there. <br /><br />So, yeah. Writing, story, characters ... Good stuff.<br /><br />There were only a couple of issues I had with this book in particular.<br /><br />1) The whole thing with Koenig ... <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[how he just conveniently believes in werewolves and is able to help them all out. It was kind of a big cop-out. No pun intended. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />2) The ending didn't leave me with much of a sense of closure. Usually when I finish a series I really like, I'm left with this powerful feeling––this cross between satisfaction and sadness that the series is over. For example, I finished reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9918083.Goliath__Leviathan___3_" title="Goliath (Leviathan, #3) by Scott Westerfeld" rel="nofollow noopener">Goliath</a> by Scott Westerfeld yesterday, and when I finished it, I was like, "OMG THAT WAS SO GOOD. BUT NOOOO IT'S OVER. *SOBS*" With <i>Forever</i>, I didn't really feel that way. It left me with more of an empty feeling, like I didn't think things had quite been tied together. I think the main issue was that it all seemed really rushed. Pretty much the whole ending happened within the last 20-30 pages or so. The first two books also had somewhat rushed endings, but at least there was more buildup to them and I found the endings more satisfactory. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[This was like, "PEOPLE SHOOTING WOLVES. Now they're gone. Beck's dead. Shelby's dead. Cole's dead. Just kidding, Cole's not dead. We're all leaving Mercy Falls. THE END." And it felt like it was all happening a bit too fast. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I also had a believability issue with the ending. I just couldn't bring myself to believe that Grace's parents would trust her to go off to Norway. I'd think they'd be pretty suspicious especially after her dad had so many issues with Sam. But, oh well. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Anyway, in the end it was a good book and I enjoyed it. I just felt it wasn't as good as the first two and didn't leave me feeling as satisfied as I wished it would. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9452109339556181034" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7395606753301864727">As I progressed through Forever, I tried to keep an open mind that it was going to get better. I had seen the mixed reviews on GR, so I did know it probability was high that I was not going to love it.<br/><br/>However, after that…that… <i>“ending”</i>, I can only cough up two stars. I really think the author was bored with this series and its characters before she attempted to write the third. This one had no emotion, and it was dare I say <i>boring</i>.<br/><br/>Likes:<br/>The covers of all three are very pretty, and if you read pa</span>
  <span id="freeText7395606753301864727" style="display:none">As I progressed through Forever, I tried to keep an open mind that it was going to get better. I had seen the mixed reviews on GR, so I did know it probability was high that I was not going to love it.<br /><br />However, after that…that… <i>“ending”</i>, I can only cough up two stars. I really think the author was bored with this series and its characters before she attempted to write the third. This one had no emotion, and it was dare I say <i>boring</i>.<br /><br />Likes:<br />The covers of all three are very pretty, and if you read paper, you get the treat of beautiful colored font. I was lucky enough to get a kindle loan from a friend for this one, so I did not have to pay for the crap—oh wait, this is my ‘like’s” area. Oh---uh, so I didn’t get to see the colored copy of Forever.<br /><br />Dislikes:<br />*The four points of view. It seemed ok in Linger because there was more going on. Isabell and Cole would break in when I would start to get interested. I didn’t give a crap what they were doing. Isabell stomps around pissed all the time, and Cole is just there.<br />*Sam and Grace, who are supposed to be soul mates, reunite after two months, and when Grace wakes up, she goes and talks to Cole first, then finds some food, and THEN looks for Sam? WTF. Anticlimactic and lame.<br />*The End SUCKS. I think she admitted to herself the book was dull, so she just gave up and said “oh well I will leave it open”. The End. <br /><br />What a rip off. <br /></span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review78093095">
  <td colspan="2">

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sjfqIEMObPXvvInQQaYS7sJIFuWigw1dqtAMvHHbdY+kwPehxv/DFNI3M8ZCG9YAJKZbuKcrLCYRT7Mzrt45yw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('as4zWY7+1PZL0cGKOOeONclkQPJsZgJGSUJmmZZ+x+x8OS7YCw97F3Zae5w7WkrbL4oNr2nOIz3y3dkWSXuLqA==')})
  }
//]]>
